struct SelectionContext<'cx, 'tcx> {\\n105:     pub infcx: &'cx InferCtxt<'tcx>,\\n106: \\n107:     /// Freshener used specifically for entries on the obligation\\n108:     /// stack. This ensures that all entries on the stack at one time\\n109:     /// will have the same set of placeholder entries, which is\\n110:     /// important for checking for trait bounds that recursively\\n111:     /// require themselves.\\n112:     freshener: TypeFreshener<'cx, 'tcx>,\\n113: \\n114:     /// If `intercrate` is set, we remember predicates which were\\n115:     /// considered ambiguous because of impls potentially added in other crates.\\n116:     /// This is used in coherence to give improved diagnostics.\\n117:     /// We don't do his until we detect a coherence error because it can\\n118:     /// lead to false overflow results (#47139) and because always\\n119:     /// computing it may negatively impact performance.\\n120:     intercrate_ambiguity_causes: Option<FxIndexSet<IntercrateAmbiguityCause<'tcx>>>,\\n121: \\n122:     /// The mode that trait queries run in, which informs our error handling\\n123:     /// policy. In essence, canonicalized queries need their errors propagated\\n124:     /// rather than immediately reported because we do not have accurate spans.\\n125:     query_mode: TraitQueryMode,\\n126: }\\n127: \\n128: // A stack that walks back up the stack frame.\\n129: struct TraitObligationStack<'prev, 'tcx> {\\n130:     obligation: &'prev PolyTraitObligation<'tcx>,\\n131: \\n132:     /// The trait predicate from `obligation` but \\\"freshened\\\" with the\\n133:     /// selection-context's freshener. Used to check for recursion.\\n134:     fresh_trait_pred: ty::PolyTraitPredicate<'tcx>,\\n135: \\n136:     /// Starts out equal to `depth` -- if, during evaluation, we\\n137:     /// encounter a cycle, then we will set this flag to the minimum\\n138:     /// depth of that cycle for all participants in the cycle. These\\n139:     /// participants will then forego caching their results. This is\\n140:     /// not the most efficient solution, but it addresses #60010. The\\n141:     /// problem we are trying to prevent:\\n142:     ///\\n143:     /// - If you have `A: AutoTrait` requires `B: AutoTrait` and `C: NonAutoTrait`\\n144:     /// - `B: AutoTrait` requires `A: AutoTrait` (coinductive cycle, ok)\\n145:     /// - `C: NonAutoTrait` requires `A: AutoTrait` (non-coinductive cycle, not ok)\\n146:     ///\\n147:     /// you don't want to cache that `B: AutoTrait` or `A: AutoTrait`\\n148:     /// is `EvaluatedToOk`; this is because they were only considered\\n149:     /// ok on the premise that if `A: AutoTrait` held, but we indeed\\n150:     /// encountered a problem (later on) with `A: AutoTrait`. So we\\n151:     /// currently set a flag on the stack node for `B: AutoTrait` (as\\n152:     /// well as the second instance of `A: AutoTrait`) to suppress\\n153:     /// caching.\\n154:     ///\\n155:     /// This is a simple, targeted fix. A more-performant fix requires\\n156:     /// deeper changes, but would permit more caching: we could\\n157:     /// basically defer caching until we have fully evaluated the\\n158:     /// tree, and then cache the entire tree at once. In any case, the\\n159:     /// performance impact here shouldn't be so horrible: every time\\n160:     /// this is hit, we do cache at least one trait, so we only\\n161:     /// evaluate each member of a cycle up to N times, where N is the\\n162:     /// length of the cycle. This means the performance impact is\\n163:     /// bounded and we shouldn't have any terrible worst-cases.\\n164:     reached_depth: Cell<usize>,\\n165: \\n166:     previous: TraitObligationStackList<'prev, 'tcx>,\\n167: \\n168:     /// The number of parent frames plus one (thus, the topmost frame has depth 1).\\n169:     depth: usize,\\n170: \\n171:     /// The depth-first number of this node in the search graph -- a\\n172:     /// pre-order index. Basically, a freshly incremented counter.\\n173:     dfn: usize,\\n174: }\\n175: \\n176: struct SelectionCandidateSet<'tcx> {\\n177:     /// A list of candidates that definitely apply to the current\\n178:     /// obligation (meaning: types unify).\\n179:     vec: Vec<SelectionCandidate<'tcx>>,\\n180: \\n181:     /// If `true`, then there were candidates that might or might\\n182:     /// not have applied, but we couldn't tell. This occurs when some\\n183:     /// of the input types are type variables, in which case there are\\n184:     /// various \\\"builtin\\\" rules that might or might not trigger.\\n185:     ambiguous: bool,\\n186: }\\n187: \\n188: #[derive(PartialEq, Eq, Debug, Clone)]\\n189: struct EvaluatedCandidate<'tcx> {\\n190:     candidate: SelectionCandidate<'tcx>,\\n191:     evaluation: EvaluationResult,\\n192: }\\n193: \\n194: impl<'cx, 'tcx> SelectionContext<'cx, 'tcx> {\\n195:     pub fn new(infcx: &'cx InferCtxt<'tcx>) -> SelectionContext<'cx, 'tcx> {\\n196:         SelectionContext {\\n197:             infcx,\\n198:             freshener: infcx.freshener(),\\n199:             intercrate_ambiguity_causes: None,\\n200:             query_mode: TraitQueryMode::Standard,\\n201: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs%3FL1-200\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"a68d9aa0-0d5d-45a7-8dc9-d18b52565b16","uuid":"34251864-5800-44c0-9e08-0d5de7a21037","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: //! Used to check for recursion.\n134:     fresh_trait_pred: ty::PolyTraitPredicate<'tcx>,\n135: \n136:     /// Starts out equal to `depth` -- if, during evaluation, we\n137:     /// encounter a cycle, then we will set this flag to the minimum\n138:     /// depth of that cycle for all participants in the cycle. These\n139:     /// participants will then forego caching their results. This is\n140:     /// not the most efficient solution, but it addresses #60010. The\n141:     /// problem we are trying to prevent:\n142:     ///\n143:     /// - If you have `A: AutoTrait` requires `B: AutoTrait` and `C: NonAutoTrait`\n144:     /// - `B: AutoTrait` requires `A: AutoTrait` (coinductive cycle, ok)\n145:     /// - `C: NonAutoTrait` requires `A: AutoTrait` (non-coinductive cycle, not ok)\n146:     ///\n147:     /// you don't want to cache that `B: AutoTrait` or `A: AutoTrait`\n148:     /// is `EvaluatedToOk`; this is because they were only considered\n149:     /// ok on the premise that if `A: AutoTrait` held, but we indeed\n150:     /// encountered a problem (later on) with `A: AutoTrait`. So we\n151:     /// currently set a flag on the stack node for `B: AutoTrait` (as\n152:     /// well as the second instance of `A: AutoTrait`) to suppress\n153:     /// caching.\n154:     ///\n155:     /// This is a simple, targeted fix. A more-performant fix requires\n156:     /// deeper changes, but would permit more caching: we could\n157:     /// basically defer caching until we have fully evaluated the\n158:     /// tree, and then cache the entire tree at once. In any case, the\n159:     /// performance impact here shouldn't be so horrible: every time\n160:     /// this is hit, we do cache at least one trait, so we only\n161:     /// evaluate each member of a cycle up to N times, where N is the\n162:     /// length of the cycle. This means the performance impact is\n163:     /// bounded and we shouldn't have any terrible worst-cases.\n164:     reached_depth: Cell<usize>,\n165: \n166:     previous: TraitObligationStackList<'prev, 'tcx>,\n167: \n168:     /// The number of parent frames plus one (thus, the topmost frame has depth 1).\n169:     depth: usize,\n170: \n171:     /// The depth-first number of this node in the search graph -- a\n172:     /// pre-order index. This occurs when some\n183:     /// of the input types are type variables, in which case there are\n184:     /// various \"builtin\" rules that might or might not trigger.\n185:     ambiguous: bool,\n186: }\n187: \n188: #[derive(PartialEq, Eq, Debug, Clone)]\n189: struct EvaluatedCandidate<'tcx> {\n190:     candidate: SelectionCandidate<'tcx>,\n191:     evaluation: EvaluationResult,\n192: }\n193: \n194: impl<'cx, 'tcx> SelectionContext<'cx, 'tcx> {\n195:     pub fn new(infcx: &'cx InferCtxt<'tcx>) -> SelectionContext<'cx, 'tcx> {\n196:         SelectionContext {\n197:             infcx,\n198:             freshener: infcx.freshener(),\n199:             intercrate_ambiguity_causes: None,\n200:             query_mode: TraitQueryMode::Standard,\n201: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs%3FL1-200"}}}

The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \\\"backtrace\\\" of each\\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\\n5: //! place).\\n6: //!\\n7: //! ### External view\\n8: //!\\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\\n11: //!\\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\\n14: //!\\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\\n24: //!\\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\\n32: //!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \\\"true\\\"\\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\\n34: //!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\\n35: //!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\\n36: //!   `process_obligations`.\\n37: //! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\\n38: //!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\\n39: //!   \\\"backtrace\\\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\\n40: //!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\\n41: //!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\\n42: //!   now considered to be in error.\\n43: //!\\n44: //! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\\n45: //! which includes two bits of information:\\n46: //!\\n47: //! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\\n48: //!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\\n49: //!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\\n50: //!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\\n51: //!   then `O` will be considered completed right away if `C` is the\\n52: //!   empty vector. Otherwise it will only be considered completed once\\n53: //!   all the obligations in `C` have been found completed.\\n54: //! - `errors`: a list of errors that occurred and associated backtraces\\n55: //!   at the time of error, which can be used to give context to the user.\\n56: //!\\n57: //! Upon completion, none of the existing obligations were *shallowly\\n58: //! successful* (that is, no callback returned `Changed(_)`). This implies that\\n59: //! all obligations were either errors or returned an ambiguous result.\\n60: //!\\n61: //! ### Implementation details\\n62: //!\\n63: //! For the most part, comments specific to the implementation are in the\\n64: //! code. This file only contains a very high-level overview. Basically,\\n65: //! the forest is stored in a vector. Each element of the vector is a node\\n66: //! in some tree. Each node in the vector has the index of its dependents,\\n67: //! including the first dependent which is known as the parent. It also\\n68: //! has a current state, described by `NodeState`. After each processing\\n69: //! step, we compress the vector to remove completed and error nodes, which\\n70: //! aren't needed anymore.\\n71: \\n72: use std::cell::Cell;\\n73: use std::collections::hash_map::Entry;\\n74: use std::fmt::Debug;\\n75: use std::hash;\\n76: use std::marker::PhantomData;\\n77: \\n78: use thin_vec::ThinVec;\\n79: use tracing::debug;\\n80: \\n81: use /// then it must be sound to use the result of processing one obligation\\n94:     /// (e.g. success for error) for the other obligation\\n95:     fn as_cache_key(&self) -> Self::CacheKey;\\n96: }\\n97: \\n98: pub trait ObligationProcessor {\\n99:     type Obligation: ForestObligation;\\n100:     type Error: Debug;\\n101:     type OUT: OutcomeTrait<Obligation = Self::Obligation, Error =    /// top**.\\n124:     ///\\n125:     /// In other words, if we had O1 which required O2 which required\\n126:     /// O3 which required O1, we would give an iterator yielding O1,\\n127:     /// O2, The `ObligationForest` is a utility data structure used in trait\n2: //! matching to track the set of outstanding obligations (those not yet\n3: //! resolved to success or error). It also tracks the \"backtrace\" of each\n4: //! pending obligation (why we are trying to figure this out in the first\n5: //! place).\n6: //!\n7: //! ### External view\n8: //!\n9: //! `ObligationForest` supports two main public operations (there are a\n10: //! few others not discussed here):\n11: //!\n12: //! 1. Add a new root obligations (`register_obligation`).\n13: //! 2. Process the pending obligations (`process_obligations`).\n14: //!\n15: //! When a new obligation `N` is added, it becomes the root of an\n16: //! obligation tree. This tree can also carry some per-tree state `T`,\n17: //! which is given at the same time. This tree is a singleton to start, so\n18: //! `N` is both the root and the only leaf. Each time the\n19: //! `process_obligations` method is called, it will invoke its callback\n20: //! with every pending obligation (so that will include `N`, the first\n21: //! time). The callback also receives a (mutable) reference to the\n22: //! per-tree state `T`. The callback should process the obligation `O`\n23: //! that it is given and return a `ProcessResult`:\n24: //!\n25: //! - `Unchanged` -> ambiguous result. Obligation was neither a success\n26: //!   nor a failure. It is assumed that further attempts to process the\n27: //!   obligation will yield the same result unless something in the\n28: //!   surrounding environment changes.\n29: //! - `Changed(C)` - the obligation was *shallowly successful*. The\n30: //!   vector `C` is a list of subobligations. The meaning of this is that\n31: //!   `O` was successful on the assumption that all the obligations in `C`\n32: //!   are also successful. Therefore, `O` is only considered a \"true\"\n33: //!   success if `C` is empty. Otherwise, `O` is put into a suspended\n34: //!   state and the obligations in `C` become the new pending\n35: //!   obligations. They will be processed the next time you call\n36: //!   `process_obligations`.\n37: //! - `Error(E)` -> obligation failed with error `E`. We will collect this\n38: //!   error and return it from `process_obligations`, along with the\n39: //!   \"backtrace\" of obligations (that is, the list of obligations up to\n40: //!   and including the root of the failed obligation). No further\n41: //!   obligations from that same tree will be processed, since the tree is\n42: //!   now considered to be in error.\n43: //!\n44: //! When the call to `process_obligations` completes, you get back an `Outcome`,\n45: //! which includes two bits of information:\n46: //!\n47: //! - `completed`: a list of obligations where processing was fully\n48: //!   completed without error (meaning that all transitive subobligations\n49: //!   have also been completed). So, for example, if the callback from\n50: //!   `process_obligations` returns `Changed(C)` for some obligation `O`,\n51: //!   then `O` will be considered completed right away if `C` is the\n52: //!   empty vector. Otherwise it will only be considered completed once\n53: //!   all the obligations in `C` have been found completed.\n54: //! - `errors`: a list of errors that occurred and associated backtraces\n55: //!   at the time of error, which can be used to give context to the user.\n56: //!\n57: //! Upon completion, none of the existing obligations were *shallowly\n58: //! successful* (that is, no callback returned `Changed(_)`). This implies that\n59: //! all obligations were either errors or returned an ambiguous result.\n60: //!\n61: //! ### Implementation details\n62: //!\n63: //! For the most part, comments specific to the implementation are in the\n64: //! code. This file only contains a very high-level overview. Basically,\n65: //! the forest is stored in a vector. Each element of the vector is a node\n66: //! in some tree. Each node in the vector has the index of its dependents,\n67: //! including the first dependent which is known as the parent. It also\n68: //! has a current state, described by `NodeState`. After each processing\n69: //! step, we compress the vector to remove completed and error nodes, which\n70: //! aren't needed anymore.\n71: \n72: use std::cell::Cell;\n73: use std::collections::hash_map::Entry;\n74: use std::fmt::Debug;\n75: use std::hash;\n76: use std::marker::PhantomData;\n77: \n78: use thin_vec::ThinVec;\n79: use tracing::debug;\n80: \n81: use crate::fx::{FxHashMap, FxHashSet};\n82: \n83: mod graphviz;\n84: \n85: #[cfg(test)]\n86: mod tests;\n87: \n88: pub trait ForestObligation: Clone + Debug {\n89:     type CacheKey: Clone + hash::Hash + Eq + Debug;\n90: \n91:     /// Converts this `ForestObligation` suitable for use as a cache key.\n92:     /// If two distinct `ForestObligations`s return the same cache key,\n93:     /// then it must be sound to use the result of processing one obligation\n94:     /// (e.g. success for error) for the other obligation\n95:     fn as_cache_key(&self) -> Self::CacheKey;\n96: }\n97: \n98: pub trait Self::Error>>;\n102: \n103:     /// Implementations can provide a fast-path to obligation-processing\n104:     /// by counting the prefix of the passed iterator for which\n105:     /// `needs_process_obligation` would return false.\n106:     fn skippable_obligations<'a>(\n107:         &'a self,\n108:         _it: impl Iterator<Item = &'a Self::Obligation>,\n109:     ) -> usize {\n110:         0\n111:     }\n112: \n113:     fn needs_process_obligation(&self, _obligation: &Self::Obligation) -> bool;\n114: \n115:     fn process_obligation(\n116:         &mut self,\n117: an actual cycle. `cycle` is an iterator that starts\n122:     /// at the start of the cycle in the stack and walks **toward the\n123:     /// top**.\n124:     ///\n125:     /// In other words, if we had O1 which required O2 which required\n126:     /// O3 which required O1, we would give an iterator yielding O1,\n127:     /// O2, O3 (O1 is not yielded twice).\n128:     fn process_backedge<'c, \n404:         let candidates = candidate_set.vec;\n405: \n406:         debug!(?stack, ?candidates, \"assembled {} candidates\", candidates.len());\n407: \n408:         // At this point, we know that each of the entries in the\n409:         // candidate set is *individually* applicable. Now we have to\n410:         // figure out if they contain mutual incompatibilities. This\n411:         // frequently arises if we have an unconstrained input type --\n412:         // for example, we are looking for `$0: Eq` where `$0` is some\n413:         // unconstrained type variable. In that case, we'll get a\n414:         // candidate which assumes $0 == int, one that assumes `$0 ==\n415:         // usize`, etc. This spells an ambiguity.\n416: \n417:         let mut candidates = self.filter_impls(candidates, stack.obligation);\n418: \n419:         // If there is more than one candidate, first winnow them down\n420:         // by considering extra conditions (nested obligations and so\n421:         // forth). We don't winnow if there is exactly one\n422:         // candidate. This is a relatively minor distinction but it\n423:         // can lead to better inference and error-reporting. An\n424:         // example would be if there was an impl:\n425:         //\n426:         //     impl<T:Clone> Vec<T> { fn push_clone(...) { ... } }\n427:         //\n428:         // and we were to see some code `foo.push_clone()` where `boo`\n429:         // is a `Vec<Bar>` and `Bar` does not implement `Clone`. If\n430:         // we were to winnow, we'd wind up with zero candidates.\n431:         // Instead, we select the right impl now but report \"`Bar` does\n432:         // not implement `Clone`\".\n433:         if candidates.len() == 1 {\n434:             return self.filter_reservation_impls(candidates.pop().unwrap());\n435:         }\n436: \n437:         // Winnow, but record the exact outcome of evaluation, which\n438:         // is needed for specialization. Propagate overflow if it occurs.\n439:         let candidates = candidates\n440:             .into_iter()\n441:             .map(|c| match self.evaluate_candidate(stack, &c) {\n442:                 Ok(eval) if eval.may_apply() => {\n443:                     Ok(Some(EvaluatedCandidate { candidate: c, evaluation: eval }))\n444:                 }\n445:                 Ok(_) => Ok(None),\n446:                 Err(OverflowError::Canonical) => {\n447:                     Err(SelectionError::Overflow(OverflowError::Canonical))\n448:                 }\n449:                 Err(OverflowError::Error(e)) => {\n450:                     Err(SelectionError::Overflow(OverflowError::Error(e)))\n451: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_trait_selection/src/traits/select/mod.rs%3FL300-450"}}}
